< Review>
I love history and this is part of ours in the USA. We were visiting family in Sacramento and took a stroll through Old Town. This is where the Pony Express ended and it started in St. Joseph (Joe) Missouri. It only lasted 18 months (April 3 1860-October 26 1861) due to the Trans-Atlantic Telegraph being completed. But in it‚Äôs heyday it they could travel on horseback 1800 miles in 10 days. Quite a feat in those days.</Review>

< Review>
This place is great.  I came into f45 after years of inconsistent workout routines and diet.  The structure of the program is essentially organized circuits of exercises that are all completed within a specified time interval (totaling to 45 minutes).  Rest periods range from 15-20 seconds in between sets, so your heart is pumping The entire time. The instructors are very helpful and encouraging and it also helps if you have a good partner to push you.  If you are like me and are in poor shape coming in, don‚Äôt be discouraged if you fail to finish a set or part of a workout.  These types of exercises are built to challenge and the goal is to continuously progress and build the endurance to finish each of these workouts.  I highly recommend this place and also highly recommend bringing a friend.< /Review>

< Text>
On a mission to buy medication for my dog.  Made purchase without difficulty.  Part of the Costco experience is window shopping and making that impulse purchase.  And so it was with that really nice leather chair.  I have been lusting for one of these.  I identified my target item, only to realize there is no price tag displayed.  Now all Costco shoppers have come to identify the price from a paper tag displayed over the item.  None to be seen.  So I checked with member services.  I explained my question and this is what I was told.  "We only put price tags on the display item and then we scatter the rest around the warehouse". Huh?  Never encountered this process before.  Seems like a weird marketing scheme.  The customer has to go on a treasure hunt seeking the display item to find the price and then go on a quest to find the non-display item to load up and purchase.  A new concept in marketing.  Make the customer go into a shopping frenzy looking for that leather chair.  Glazed over eyes tongue hanging out in anticipation of riding this leather chariot to my living room.  I found the whole thing non-Costco and slightly anti-customer. It's kind of obstruction marketing. Is the idea that you will appreciate the chair more if you had to work for it.  I had a couple of dates like that in high school.  A little miffed I got a swirl yogurt.  I didn't have to chase it and the price was prominently displayed.  In the future my shopping mantra will be 'AMAZON'!</Text>

<date>1465890228083</date>< review>
What's NOT to love! I can safely say that if I was allowed to exclusively visit ONE store only and no other...it would be Costco!!! Saturdays are super busy but that's my day of choice regardless of the longer lines. Their organic section is fabulous and their meat and poultry are fresh, hormone free and delicious! If you go early enough...there's a fair bit of food sampling going on, however this tends to vary from day to day. Their mixed unsalted nuts are a show stopper at $17.99 (cashews, almonds, pecans, and pistachios). Not a lot of vegan options yet unfortunately, and a lot of their vitamins and supplements are full of fillers - hence I recommend either Whole Foods or Trader Joe's for those! Having said that, their Megared Krill Oil and the Kirkland brand co-enzyme Q10 capsules are awesome.<//review>
